### 4.H2604.989-001 — H2604 · group `989-001`

| Field | Value |
|---|---|
| context_description | Term names mercy shown in moral action and the plea of prayer — the practice of mercy toward the oppressed and the inner posture of petition before God |
| dimension | 06 — Relational Disposition |
| dimension_confidence | CLAUDE_AI |
| dominant_subject | HUMAN |
| manual_override | 0 |
| anchor / related / set-aside | 2 / 0 / 0 |
| notes | Mercy shown toward the oppressed and the inner posture of petition — the relational orientation of mercy directed outward (toward the oppressed) and upward (toward God). Automated label Moral Character captures the practice-of-mercy dimension but the group spans both the outward expression of mercy and the inward posture of petition, making Relational Disposition more precise. ### 4.H3722A.3169-001 — H3722A · group `3169-001`

| Field | Value |
|---|---|
| context_description | Term names the priestly/ritual act by which human guilt is covered before God and forgiveness granted — atonement as the mechanism addressing the person's moral condition |
| dimension | 10 — Dependence / Creatureliness |
| dimension_confidence | CLAUDE_AI |
| dominant_subject | HUMAN |
| manual_override | 0 |
| anchor / related / set-aside | 2 / 58 / 12 |
| notes | The priestly atoning act that addresses human guilt before God — the creature's condition of moral accountability before the Creator addressed through the atonement mechanism. Automated label Moral Character is partial (it names the moral condition addressed) but misses the constitutive dimension: the atonement system reveals and addresses the creature's fundamental condition of guilt-before-God, |

|---|---|
| context_description | Term names a substitutionary price paid for a life — ransom as the means by which moral accountability for life is addressed before God or human authority |
| dimension | 10 — Dependence / Creatureliness |
| dimension_confidence | CLAUDE_AI |
| dominant_subject | HUMAN |
| manual_override | 0 |
| anchor / related / set-aside | 2 / 8 / 0 |
| notes | The ransom as the mechanism addressing the creature's moral accountability for life — the human person absolutely dependent on a divinely found price. Automated label Moral Character captures the moral accountability dimension but misses the primary inner-being characteristic: the creature's absolute dependence on a provision beyond human capacity. Correcting to Dependence/Creatureliness. |

### 6.1 Universal catalogue (223 questions)

#### Compassion Extensions

| Code | Pattern | Question |
|---|---|---|
| `C-001` | — | Does the evidence for the word include a significant cluster of prohibition contexts — and if so, what does the frequency of the word's prohibition reveal about its default status in the inner being? |
| `C-002` | — | Does any verse depict the word winning an inner contest with a competing disposition — and if so, what does this reveal about the word's relationship to other inner-being characteristics that it must overcome? |
| `C-003` | — | Does the evidence assign the word an explicitly everlasting or permanent temporal character — in direct contrast to the momentary character of a competing or opposing disposition? |
| `C-004` | — | Is the word's abstract meaning etymologically derived from a concrete somatic reality — and if so, what does this unusual etymological direction reveal about the relationship between the inner experience and its bodily ground? |
| `C-005` | — | Does the word have a participatory dimension — does it operate as genuine entry into another's experience rather than response from a safe distance — and if so, does this participation carry an eschatological trajectory? |
| `C-006` | — | Does any verse name the violation of the word by the very person who most characteristically bears it — and if so, what does this reveal about the word's resilience or fragility under external pressure? |
| `C-007` | — | Has the word acquired a standardised or institutionalised social form — a normative outward expression that names what the characteristic looks like when it is embodied in social practice? |
| `C-008` | — | Does the word identify a specific category of person who needs it but cannot perceive their own need — and what conditions produce the failure of need-recognition? |

| `Q061` | — | How does a key verse handle the co-presence of genuine human effort and prior divine initiative? |

| `Q064` | — | Does a key verse describe the word's work as directed toward the present only, or toward a future state? |
| `Q065` | — | Does any verse distinguish between a performed version and a genuine version of the word? |
| `Q066` | — | What inner orientation does a key verse identify as the source of the genuine quality? |
| `Q067` | — | What is the sequence of somatic and verbal response in a key verse — which comes first? |
| `Q068` | — | What does a recipient's response in a key verse reveal about their inner experience of receiving the word? |
| `Q069` | — | What structural condition in a key verse establishes the recipient as having no basis for the word they receive? |
| `Q070` | — | In a key verse, does the word operate within or across existing relational, covenantal, or social boundaries? |
| `Q071` | — | What is the logical structure of a key argument about the word — and what is its premise and conclusion? |
| `Q072` | — | What inner-being state does the argument structure in a key verse produce in the recipient? |

#### Section 5 — Connections and Research Pointers

| Code | Pattern | Question |
|---|---|---|
| `Q122` | — | What is the strongest co-occurrence connection for this word — which adjacent characteristic appears most frequently in the same verses — and what does the co-occurrence pattern reveal? |
| `Q123` | — | Does any verse indicate that this word and its most closely connected adjacent characteristic operate simultaneously in the same inner-being moment — and what would that simultaneity imply? |
| `Q124` | — | What are the three highest vocabulary-sharing registries for this word — and what does the pattern of sharing reveal about the word's structural position in the programme? |
| `Q125` | — | Does the vocabulary overlap with any adjacent characteristic extend to root-level architecture — a shared root rather than only shared individual terms? |
| `Q126` | — | How many of this word's confirmed analytical dimensions are shared with another cluster or characteristic — and is there any cluster that shares all confirmed dimensions? |
| `Q127` | — | Does any single verse make an explicit structural relationship between this word and an adjacent characteristic — naming the connection rather than merely exemplifying it? |
| `Q128` | — | What is the co-occurrence count between this word and the characteristic with which it shares the most anchor verses — and what does that shared anchoring reveal? |
| `Q129` | — | Where this word and an adjacent characteristic share a dominant directionality (such as both being primarily divine-to-human), what does the shared directionality reveal about their structural relationship? |
| `Q130` | — | What is the relationship between this word and human will in the verse evidence — does the word displace, bypass, or reconstitute the will? |
| `Q131` | — | How does the study describe the relationship between this word and calling — is calling a consequence, an expression, or a distinct phenomenon? |
| `Q132` | — | What inner-being posture connects this word and listening — and is that posture described as a precondition or an expression of the word? |
| `Q133` | — | How does the study distinguish this word from faith — and what is their structural relationship? |
| `Q134` | — | What is the described sequence from the word to peace — and what comes between them? |
| `Q135` | — | What is the vocabulary overlap and co-occurrence count between this word and guilt? |
| `Q136` | — | What is the relationship between this word and mourning — does mourning precede, follow, or accompany the word? |
| `Q137` | — | Does the study present this word and hope as two separate phenomena or as aspects of a single inner-being posture? |
| `Q138` | — | Does any verse function as a primary anchor in both this word's study and another word's study — and what does that dual membership reveal about their relationship? |
| `Q139` | — | Does any verse anchor both this word and another word — and what shared inner-being posture does that dual anchoring reveal? |
| `Q140` | — | Does any verse present adjacent qualities as aspects of a unified inner-being posture — and if so, what is their common source? |
| `Q141` | — | What functional overlap does the verse evidence suggest between this word and wisdom? |
| `Q142` | — | Does the word operate only in relation to moral conditions (guilt) or also in relation to conditions of incapacity — and what is the evidence? |
| `Q143` | — | What is the co-occurrence count between this word and goodness — and in what literary context does the pairing appear? |
| `Q144` | — | What is the co-occurrence count between this word and anointing, and between this word and blessing? |
| `Q145` | — | Is the connection between this word and forgiveness established through contextual inference or through the lexical form of the term itself? |
| `Q146` | — | Does the verse evidence in this study point toward a connection with repentance — and is that connection sufficiently examined or deferred? |
| `Q147` | — | Does a recurring posture appear across the word-seeking scenes in the study — and is its relationship to an adjacent characteristic examined or deferred? |

|---|---|---|
